    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer6279109055184713366">Mara is a proud and beautiful slave girl who yearns for freedom. In order to gain it, she finds herself playing the dangerous role of double spy for two arch enemies—each of whom supports a contender for the throne of Egypt.<br/><br/>Against her will, Mara finds herself falling in love with one of her masters, the noble Sheftu, and she starts to believe in his plans of restoring Thu</span>
  <span id="freeText6279109055184713366" style="display:none">Mara is a proud and beautiful slave girl who yearns for freedom. In order to gain it, she finds herself playing the dangerous role of double spy for two arch enemies—each of whom supports a contender for the throne of Egypt.<br /><br />Against her will, Mara finds herself falling in love with one of her masters, the noble Sheftu, and she starts to believe in his plans of restoring Thutmose III to the throne. But just when Mara is ready to offer Sheftu her help and her heart, her duplicity is discovered, and a battle ensues in which both Mara's life and the fate of Egypt are at stake.</span>

<div id='communityQuestionsWithAnswers'>
<div class='communityQuestionAndAnswer'>
<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/1290527-is-this-book-historically-accurate">Is this book historically accurate? Wikipedia says that Hatshepsut was the chief wife of Thutmose II and Thutmose III was her stepson. (not half-brother as this book portrays)
I also didn&#39;t find any information on her bankrupting the treasury. She is mostly described as a strong, powerful and successful pharaoh, very much unlike the selfish and sinister woman in this book.</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>

</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/49755553-rebecca">Rebecca</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">This is an old thread, but I wanted to weigh in. This book was written in the 50s. As a result we didn't actually know much about Hatshepsut when this<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">This is an old thread, but I wanted to weigh in. This book was written in the 50s. As a result we didn't actually know much about Hatshepsut when this books was written. So take the historical accuracy with a grain of salt, but please keep in mind that the author was trying her best to be accurate with the knowledge that was available to her at the time, <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

<div id="review_826496878" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/826496878" />
    <a title="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8734459-tadiana-night-owl"><img alt="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603085284p2/8734459.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/826496878?book_show_action=true">Jan 17, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" href="/user/show/8734459-tadiana-night-owl">Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=you-go-girl-kickass-heroine">you-go-girl-kickass-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=comfort-read">comfort-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=squeaky-clean-romance">squeaky-clean-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=oldies-but-goodies">oldies-but-goodies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=egypt">egypt</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer826496878" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7372325257637025966"><i>Mara, Daughter of the Nile</i> holds up amazingly well for a 60+ year old YA book. Set in ancient Egypt, it's the story of Mara, a bright, feisty slave girl who unexpectedly finds herself forced to act as a spy for <u>both</u> sides of a conflict over the throne of Egypt. Either side is likely to immediately kill her if her duplicity is discovered. And then her heart starts to get involved ...<br/><br/>I had very fond memories of reading Mara years ago, and I was delighted and, frankly, relieved when my re-read live</span>
  <span id="freeText7372325257637025966" style="display:none"><i>Mara, Daughter of the Nile</i> holds up amazingly well for a 60+ year old YA book. Set in ancient Egypt, it's the story of Mara, a bright, feisty slave girl who unexpectedly finds herself forced to act as a spy for <u>both</u> sides of a conflict over the throne of Egypt. Either side is likely to immediately kill her if her duplicity is discovered. And then her heart starts to get involved ...<br /><br />I had very fond memories of reading Mara years ago, and I was delighted and, frankly, relieved when my re-read lived up to my memories, which isn't always the case when I re-read favorite books from my teenage years. (*cough<i>robertheinlein</i>cough*) It's not a perfect book, but I'm upping my rating to five stars, dang it, just because I can, and because I so enjoyed Mara and her duel of wits with Sheftu. Sheftu is my favorite kind of book hero, an intelligent, extremely capable man hiding behind the mask of a charming, lazy courtier in order to achieve a greater goal. (I'm such a sucker for that Scarlet Pimpernel kind of trope.)<blockquote>Tomorrow, by Amon, she would have revenge. She would treat him with a smiling indifference he wouldn't be able to break through no matter how hard he tried. She would be gay--aye, charming--but oh, how remote! . . .<br /><br />Mara found Sheftu's manner the next morning just as gay, just as impersonal, and so much more convincing than her own that she was out of sorts before an hour had passed. There was no outdoing him at irony, that was clear. She would have to find some other means of punishing him.</blockquote>But this is more than a simple adventure and love story; the book has some surprisingly profound ideas about living for a greater cause, the power of love for your country, and how a country is made up of people, the poor and humble as well as the rich and powerful ― all of whom are important.<br /><br />This one's a keeper and a total comfort read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7372325257637025966" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_481482333" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/481482333" />
    <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies"><img alt="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500999223p2/4527753.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/481482333?book_show_action=true">Dec 19, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies">Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=all-time-favorites">all-time-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=nobility">nobility</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=middle-school">middle-school</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=mythology">mythology</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=kick-ass-heroine">kick-ass-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=historical">historical</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer481482333" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18319922012005737602"><blockquote>
  <b>"Then the stars went out, for the bark of Ra, in fiery splendor, burst out of the East. Sunshine flooded the wide desert and the long, green valley of the Nile. The night was over; a new day has dawned for the land of Egypt."</b>
</blockquote>Generally, I do not reread books. I have a short attention span, I constantly seek novelty, and once a book or a film has been watched, even if I greatly enjoyed it, I will never reach for it again. There are only a few books that I enjoy rereading, <i>Mara, Daughter of the</i></span>
  <span id="freeText18319922012005737602" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>"Then the stars went out, for the bark of Ra, in fiery splendor, burst out of the East. Sunshine flooded the wide desert and the long, green valley of the Nile. The night was over; a new day has dawned for the land of Egypt."</b>
</blockquote>Generally, I do not reread books. I have a short attention span, I constantly seek novelty, and once a book or a film has been watched, even if I greatly enjoyed it, I will never reach for it again. There are only a few books that I enjoy rereading, <i>Mara, Daughter of the Nile</i> has been one I have reached for repeatedly since I first read it and fell in love with it as a 12-year old girl. A few years ago, I donated a enormous amount of books after reluctantly admitting to myself that I will never touch them again after the initial reading: this book still occupies a place on my currently tiny and trimmed-down collection of paperbacks, and it's going nowhere.<br /><br />Call it nostalgia, if you will, but this is such a lovely little book, and it has occupied a dear space in my heart ever since. This is a solidly middle-grade novel, but I find that <b>a great middle-grade novel is a wonderful thing</b>. They are so essential to hook in a young reader and instill in them a love of reading that lasts a lifetime. These books have themes, they have believable, loveable, flawed characters. There's no psychoanalysis required of the characters, but they send such an important message to a young reader: you can be better than you think, you can be a good person, you can aim for higher than what you believe yourself capable. <b>A small person can make a difference.</b><br /><br />The story is simple, the plot is straightforward. There is no overwhelming theme here of existence, no aspirations to grandeur, yet I love it just the same. I do confess to being a great fan of Ancient Egypt. The mythology, the people, the history; while I have read many books within this setting, telling stories of such exalted characters as Cleopatra, Nefertiti, King Tutankhamen, this wee book <b>remains my favorite in the sadly rare genre of Egyptian fiction</b>.<br /><br />Mara is a slave, she was not always one, but that has been her life for as long as she can remember. She is a foreign-born slave, captured with her late mother; Mara has blue eyes, which is reviled and feared by her master, and is different from most slaves in that she has been previously educated in reading and writing. She also has a more valuable commodity: the ability to speak Babylonian. It is for this purpose that Queen Hatshepsut's man initially buys her; she is to spy upon Prince Thutmose through his future bride. Mara is to play the interpreter for Princess the Canaanite princess, Inanni.<br /><br />Through a twist of fate, Mara ends up playing the unwilling double agent, with none the wiser. She ends up being a pawn for Lord Sheftu, who is working secretly in support of placing Prince Thutmose on the throne in place of his devious, destructive pharaoh sister, Queen Hatshepsut.<br /><br />Mara has no choice. She cannot reveal her role to either. To do so would be to risk death, truly, for the life of a slave is worth absolutely nothing to such powerful and wealthy men. Eventually, though, Mara has to choose a side, and one of her masters will prove himself to be a truly idealistic man, who is working towards a better future for Egypt. To get to her happy ending, Mara must rely on her own wits throughout the intrigue, throughout the danger. She has to overcome her own prejudices, and decide <b>whether luxury and freedom is preferable to doing what she knows is right</b>...despite the fact that it could cost her everything, including her life.<br /><br />I loved Mara's determination. Yes, she is selfish initially, but this is a girl who has been a slave, mistreated, ill-fed, feared for her freakish colored eyes, of all things. She has endured hardship, beating, and so when she is given a chance at freedom, she takes it. And boy does she love what that little taste of freedom has to bring. <br /><blockquote>
  <i>"[The clothes] were not too lavish...but to her it was unimaginable luxury. And as she shook the garments out one by one and looked at them, she felt again the fierce determination that nothing, nobody must stand in the way of her possessing such things always, freedom and gold and a life worth living---gardens with lotus blooming in the fishpool...rows and rows of papyrus scrolls on the shelves in a beautiful room.<br />So she dreamed."</i>
</blockquote>Mara is not perfect; despite being a slave, she feels herself to be a true Egyptian, and looks down upon the foreign princess Inanni. Mara is patronizing towards Inanni's full figure, which is admired by her people, but reviled by the Egyptians, who prefer a slim silhouette. Inanni's strange clothes, her customs, her fear towards anything Egyptian is viewed condescendingly by the haughty Mara. Eventually, Mara grows to realize her own faults, and realizes that she has been underestimating her princess' strengths. <br /><br />There is some romance in here, nothing too steamy, nothing inappropriate at all for the middle-grade audience. It grows step by step, there is no insta-love, as enemies grow to be friends, and then perhaps something more.<br /><br />I absolutely loved the bits of Egyptian culture in this book. The descriptions of food, of customs, of cosmetics and clothing, of daily minutiae. I don't find that the adult novels of this nature does so well in the descriptions of little details as this one did. <br /><br />The writing is beautiful, the speech pattern is strange, in some way, but does not feel out of place in this setting; I actually really loved the formal, slightly archaic quality of the speech in this book. The descriptions are beautifully described, in the way that Eloise McGraw does so well in all her children's books.<br /><br /><b>Highly recommended for anyone, of any age.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="18319922012005737602" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1375405040" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1375405040" />
    <a title="Sarah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45261627-sarah"><img alt="Sarah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1475352701p2/45261627.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1375405040?book_show_action=true">May 15, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah" href="/user/show/45261627-sarah">Sarah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45261627-sarah?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45261627-sarah?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45261627-sarah?shelf=a-fine-romance">a-fine-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45261627-sarah?shelf=actual-people-of-color-in-ya">actual-people-of-color-in-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45261627-sarah?shelf=the-desert">the-desert</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45261627-sarah?shelf=heartthrobs-and-heroes">heartthrobs-and-heroes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45261627-sarah?shelf=classics">classics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45261627-sarah?shelf=actual-chaste-romance-in-ya">actual-chaste-romance-in-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45261627-sarah?shelf=pretty-pink-cover">pretty-pink-cover</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45261627-sarah?shelf=way-down-in-egypt">way-down-in-egypt</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1375405040" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16704781344986714046"><i>Egypt, mid-1400s B.C. – </i><br/><br/>Mara calls herself “the daughter of Nobody and Nothing.” She has been a slave for as long as she can remember, but her pale eyes and ability to speak Babylonian suggest that once she was free—and did not come from Egypt. Now in her late teens, she’s endured a succession of cruel and ignorant masters. She yearns, above all else, for freedom. <br/><br/>Freedom comes—with a steep price. Mara is purchased by a nobleman in Queen Hatshepsut’s inner circle. He needs a spy to report on the</span>
  <span id="freeText16704781344986714046" style="display:none"><i>Egypt, mid-1400s B.C. – </i><br /><br />Mara calls herself “the daughter of Nobody and Nothing.” She has been a slave for as long as she can remember, but her pale eyes and ability to speak Babylonian suggest that once she was free—and did not come from Egypt. Now in her late teens, she’s endured a succession of cruel and ignorant masters. She yearns, above all else, for freedom. <br /><br />Freedom comes—with a steep price. Mara is purchased by a nobleman in Queen Hatshepsut’s inner circle. He needs a spy to report on the Queen’s brother, Thutmose, who might be planning a rebellion. If Mara betrays her master’s plans, her death is assured.<br /><br />On the barge that will bring her to the royal city, Mara falls in with Sheftu, a young nobleman close to Prince Thutmose. Sheftu is part of the planned rebellion. He offers Mara, whom he thinks is just a runaway slave with no agenda, two options—spy <i>for</i> Prince Thutmose, or face death.<br /> <br />So this devious young lady finds herself a double agent, caught between two sides that will stake everything on keeping or gaining the throne. At first, it seems like a grand game. Mara gets to be an interpreter for a visiting foreign princess. For the first time in her life, she’ll have enough food, not to mention nice clothes, scrolls to read, and an unlimited supply of eyeliner (a quality-of-life issue for every ancient Egyptian). It helps that Sheftu is unconventionally handsome, with a witty, enigmatic mode of flirting that Mara finds enthralling.<br /><br />But the deeper Mara gets into these parallel intrigues, she realizes that she’s already chosen a side…she’s lost her loyalty and her heart, and is now soon to die a traitor’s death.<br /><br /><b>Content Advisory</b><br /><br /><i>Violence</i>: A slave is beaten in the early chapters of the story, and a bloody, near-fatal beating occurs near the end. A guard is quickly slain when he tries to alert authorities to a group of rebels lawbreaking. Characters mention being impaled on stakes or thrown to the Nile’s crocodiles, but we don’t see any such executions occur in the story. Someone is forced to imbibe poison, out of view of the POV characters.<br /><br /><i>Sex</i>: The Canaanite princess, Inanni, is scandalized by Egyptian fashions—the women wear translucent sheath dresses and the men usually wear naught but kilts. <br /><br /><i>Language</i>: Nothing.<br /><br /><i>Substance Abuse</i>: Some background characters get drunk.<br /><br /><i>Politics and Religion</i>: Fleeting moments of Egyptians showing ethnic prejudice against non-Egyptians. Various Egyptian gods are casually mentioned. We don’t hear much about them, and frankly none of the characters appear to believe in them strongly. Except for that head-scratching part where the POV shifts to Nut, the night-sky goddess, injecting a fantastical note into an otherwise very grounded narrative.<br /><br /><i>Nightmare Fuel</i>: Let me put it this way—if you suffer from a fear of being trapped underground, there is a chapter in this book that you might find troubling. Some rebels break into a tomb, risking the death penalty for blasphemy if caught, to retrieve an item for the prince, <i>and their torch goes out</i>…in a room far underground full of creepy tomb paintings and guardian statues. Boy, that chapter was tense.<br /><br /><b>Conclusions</b><br />This book does not bat a thousand for historical accuracy—Hatshepsut was actually Thutmose III’s stepmother, not his half-sister as portrayed here. In real life, she died at age fifty of bone cancer after several years of poor health, a far cry from the coup and Socratic suicide portrayed in the novel. In fairness to McGraw, a lot of this information wasn’t available at the time that this book was published (1953). <br /><br />That said, while the book is not flawless as a history lesson, it is near perfect as a classic YA spy novel with a strong and clever heroine, royal intrigue, romance, and an evocative historical setting. <br />Mara was hard to like at first. While it was understandable that her hard life had made her bitter and closed-off, the flippancy with which she treated her role was bothersome, as was her mean thoughts directed at Inanni and the other foreigners. The more Mara grew to care about Egypt, the more likeable she became. McGraw set up this seemingly heartless character and then yanked the heart from her chest. The last few chapters were nail-biters, because Mara finally understood what she stood to lose. Well done.<br /><br />Sheftu is just my type of hero—witty, charismatic, always three steps ahead of his enemies, good-looking in an offbeat way, and both more principled and more caring than he lets on. The blogger at You, Me, and a Cup of Tea compared the dynamic between Sheftu and Mara to that between Han Solo and Princess Leia, albeit he’s the aristocrat and she’s the seemingly amoral, self-serving scoundrel/guttersnipe. Although Sheftu is definitely a nerf-herder. I can picture him sitting down for a drink with Eugenides, Howl, Jareth, George Cooper, Han Alister, and Morpheus the Netherling, and they would have a blast, rearranging the world and commiserating about their terrifying wives.<br /> <br />Ancient Egypt is an inherently fascinating culture. While the Mesopotamians fought amongst themselves and the Greeks were still figuring out how to read, Egypt kept doing what it always did—live along the Nile, build magnificent structures, watch the stars, and perseverate about Death. There’s a sense of timelessness, stability, and inexorability about their myths and their art and their artifacts that no other civilization can match. You can tell that McGraw loved Egypt, and her characters seem organic to the place.<br /><br />Recommended warmly for fans of <i>The Witch of Blackbird Pond, The Bronze Bow, The Sherwood Ring, The Perilous Gard, Johnny Tremain,</i> and Rosemary Sutcliff’s Roman Britain novels. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16704781344986714046" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_744596015" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/744596015" />
    <a title="Willow " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4529669-willow"><img alt="Willow " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1472180488p2/4529669.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/744596015?book_show_action=true">Oct 19, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Willow " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Willow " href="/user/show/4529669-willow">Willow </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4529669-willow?shelf=egypt">egypt</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer744596015" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7636490242263160573">Thanks for the buddy read, Jeannette! :D<br/><br/><i>Mara Daughter of the Nile</i> was originally published back in 1953, and I find that books that were written during that time, always make me think of old movies. It’s the way the characters talk and interact with each other. The hero doesn’t just kiss the heroine. He pulls her into his arms and gives her a grand sweeping kiss that should have music playing in the background. Now don’t get me wrong, I happen to love this because I think it’s breathlessly roman</span>
  <span id="freeText7636490242263160573" style="display:none">Thanks for the buddy read, Jeannette! :D<br /><br /><i>Mara Daughter of the Nile</i> was originally published back in 1953, and I find that books that were written during that time, always make me think of old movies. It’s the way the characters talk and interact with each other. The hero doesn’t just kiss the heroine. He pulls her into his arms and gives her a grand sweeping kiss that should have music playing in the background. Now don’t get me wrong, I happen to love this because I think it’s breathlessly romantic. It’s like they put every bit of sexual tension and wrapped it up in that one kiss. I can’t help but think though that it’s a characteristic of that time period, which sort of dates it. <br /><br />And like an old movie, the book moved a little bit slower. The middle dragged. This is why I knocked a star. I think the writing is lovely though.<br /><br />I liked the characters, especially Mara and Inanni and their friendship.<br /><br />I have to commend Eloise Jarvis McGraw for her excellent research and the descriptive way she brings ancient Egypt to life. McGraw adds all these lovely details, which made me think of old Egyptian art and artifacts. Although I’m much more of a Hatshepsut fangirl than McGraw is. In fact, I felt a little like Mara was helping the wrong side, because let’s face it, Hatshepsut was awesome. Sheftu argues that the Queen spends too much money on buildings, but what does he want to do, build up the army so they can go raid the borders. Whatever, Sheftu. Let’s face it, guys, you’re just annoyed that the Pharaoh is a woman, a very successful woman. <br /><br />But anyway, I did enjoy this and highly recommend it to ancient Egypt fans. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7636490242263160573" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_269128885" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/269128885" />
    <a title="laurel [the suspected bibliophile]" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7494844-laurel-the-suspected-bibliophile"><img alt="laurel [the suspected bibliophile]" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1546974316p2/7494844.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/269128885?book_show_action=true">Jun 01, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="laurel [the suspected bibliophile]" class="user" itemprop="url" name="laurel [the suspected bibliophile]" href="/user/show/7494844-laurel-the-suspected-bibliophile">laurel [the suspected bibliophile]</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7494844-laurel-the-suspected-bibliophile?shelf=2019-read">2019-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7494844-laurel-the-suspected-bibliophile?shelf=historical-fic">historical-fic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7494844-laurel-the-suspected-bibliophile?shelf=ya-books">ya-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer269128885" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5412142861753214237">Mara—ambitious and intelligent slave—gets caught up in a scheme to dethrone the pharaoh Hatshepsut while serving as an interpreter to the pharaoh's half-brother Thutmose. Yet Mara finds herself drawn to one side more than the other, particularly towards a handsome noble.<br/><br/>To be honest, I skimmed the last half of this book. It was so overly wordy and unnecessarily detailed with Mara doing dumb shit and being treated like a silly girl or the wiliest seductress that ever lived that I was tired of the</span>
  <span id="freeText5412142861753214237" style="display:none">Mara—ambitious and intelligent slave—gets caught up in a scheme to dethrone the pharaoh Hatshepsut while serving as an interpreter to the pharaoh's half-brother Thutmose. Yet Mara finds herself drawn to one side more than the other, particularly towards a handsome noble.<br /><br />To be honest, I skimmed the last half of this book. It was so overly wordy and unnecessarily detailed with Mara doing dumb shit and being treated like a silly girl or the wiliest seductress that ever lived that I was tired of the whiplash—and exhausted by the constant references to her blue eyes. <br /><br />I get it. <br /><br />Her eyes are blue. <br /><br />I don't need to be reminded of that at least once a page for...280-something pages.<br /><br />This read like it was written in the 1950s, because it was. Lots of fatphobic statements, particularly about the Syrian princess Inanni and her ladies in waiting, and lots of commentary on skin color.<br /><br />Also, the relationship between Sheftu and Mara was...cringe-worthy at best.<br /><br />Aside from her eyes and her beauty, Mara wavers between being keenly intelligent, a fluttery ingenue, a wily politician, a sultry seductress and a dumb as shit 1950s trope. Like I said earlier—the transitions and unevenness in her character were enough to give me whiplash, and I was constantly struggling to figure out her motivation for playing both sides up the middle because 1) that never works and 2) she holds literally no cards in this poker game. Remove Mara, and the book basically continues without her.<br /><br />And finally, I think I'm just tired of the evil queen tropes, as this plays with the propaganda that Hatshepsut was an awful, vainglorious and bitchy ruler who was rightfully deposed by her half-brother, who returned the country from turning inwards into building temple after temple and ruining the wealth of Egypt instead of focusing on conquering new lands and peoples. <br /><br />In this book, Hatshepsut is reviled for her coldness and haughtiness (I mean, she is the physical reincarnation of the sun god...what exactly do you expect?) and being a woman ruler, while her asshole half-brother Thutmose is a <i>caged lion</i>, filled with anger, charisma and intelligence...and a heavy dose of the same heavy-handed brutality his sister has.<br /><br />They are pretty much two halves of the same coin.<br /><br />Guess who is celebrated for their traits and who isn't?<br /><br />Guessguessguessguessguess.<br /><br />So yeah. This just made me tired.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5412142861753214237" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer3606396892981745584">I adored this book when I first read it at age 10, and still love it 20 years later. I cannot recommend it highly enough to young lady readers who have any interest at all in Ancient Egypt. <br/><br/>Mara is a slave girl sold to become a spy who ends up embroiled in a plot to overthrow the (female) Pharaoh Hatshepsut. McGraw's attention to detail and knowledge of the time are impeccable, her characters are alive and engaging, there's a nice little romance, plenty of drama and suffering for the cause, and </span>
  <span id="freeText3606396892981745584" style="display:none">I adored this book when I first read it at age 10, and still love it 20 years later. I cannot recommend it highly enough to young lady readers who have any interest at all in Ancient Egypt. <br /><br />Mara is a slave girl sold to become a spy who ends up embroiled in a plot to overthrow the (female) Pharaoh Hatshepsut. McGraw's attention to detail and knowledge of the time are impeccable, her characters are alive and engaging, there's a nice little romance, plenty of drama and suffering for the cause, and Mara is spunky in a very modern vampire slayer kind of way. Well ahead of it's time.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer764878544" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer14496792127761133910">I'll not write a long review since others have already said everything there is to be said, but I will say that I can't believe how beautiful this was. I wish I could read it all over again. Five Stars easy, it was a million times better than my last book.<br/><br/>Mara was a delight, she was a sweet little trickster who didn't know which people to side with. Whichever side she chose to spy for, there was danger and intrigue. From robing the dead in their crypts' to appearing before Pharaoh, Mara gets ent</span>
  <span id="freeText14496792127761133910" style="display:none">I'll not write a long review since others have already said everything there is to be said, but I will say that I can't believe how beautiful this was. I wish I could read it all over again. Five Stars easy, it was a million times better than my last book.<br /><br />Mara was a delight, she was a sweet little trickster who didn't know which people to side with. Whichever side she chose to spy for, there was danger and intrigue. From robing the dead in their crypts' to appearing before Pharaoh, Mara gets entangled in it all. She plays both sides, but what will she do when both realize her duplicity? <br /><br />This book was so much better than I'd thought it would be, I was afraid it would have a modern feel to it, but instead, I felt that I was right next to Mara, doing my utmost to outwit them all. I think this book is timeless.<br /><br />Did I say it <i>was</i> beautiful? It <i>is</i> beautiful. <br /><br /><b>G rating</b> There is, of course, the Egyptian Gods and Burials pomp also there is a whipping at the end, which is not described in a sickening way. Still, it was never shoved in your face.</span>

  <span id="freeText17236830042448771256" style="display:none">Mara intently fixed her gaze on the young man before her, who asked, "What is the message, Blue Eyed One?"<br /><br />"'What are your thoughts?'" she quoted. "'Shall you tell me of the plot? Have you found the writings favorable?'"<br /><br />Sheftu, with a casual smile that was yet guarded, replied, "Are those his words, or yours?"<br /><br />"By the Feather of Truth, I only quoted them exactly."<br /><br />"From your thoughts, no doubt."<br /><br /><i>Ai</i>, he knows, but I will not let him best me, thought Mara. I will get the truth of him.... "Is this book to you so slight compared to others you have had before?"<br /><br />"Nay, not in the least!"<br /><br />Mara raised her brows slightly. Other than his eyes, which glittered with amusement, the careless smile that returned to Sheftu's face did not tell he knew he had been neatly trapped. Instead of changing the subject, he went on as if his outburst had not been a mistake. "There were many things that brought it above the rest. Intrigue, betrayal, adventure, romance.... All these things combined made the reading—enjoyable."<br /><br />Inwardly, Mara sighed irritably, but did not show her frustration outwardly. <i>Ai</i>, "enjoyable"! Sheftu was surely a rogue, as Nekonkh had pointed out before, just not the kind of rogue he referred to. "But what of your opinion, Sashai?"<br /><br />"My opinion of it—is as my opinion of you, guttersnipe, my lovely Mara."<br /><br />Mara put on an innocent expression. "What is your opinion of me, pray?"<br /><br />Sheftu drew her close, his eyes traveling her face, and Mara’s heart pounded faster. "That thou are my beloved, Lotus-Eyed One," he said slowly, gently. He fingered the lotus in Mara's hair.       <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="twice_baked✌️" class="user" itemprop="url" name="twice_baked✌️" href="/user/show/46744526-twice-baked">twice_baked✌️</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1816409441" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer430075671076880849">This book is better than five stars. Honestly, I couldn't love a book more. One of the first books I ever truly <i>loved</i>, it gets better every time you read it.<br/><br/>A very sweet, complicated story about Hatshepsut's reign and ultimate overthrow. And Mara's right in the middle of it, juggling her life and the lives of others that she likes (and, maybe, dislikes). She's desperate for good luck, her whole life has been "grab it before somebody else does", "finders keepers", and she slowly realizes througho</span>
  <span id="freeText430075671076880849" style="display:none">This book is better than five stars. Honestly, I couldn't love a book more. One of the first books I ever truly <i>loved</i>, it gets better every time you read it.<br /><br />A very sweet, complicated story about Hatshepsut's reign and ultimate overthrow. And Mara's right in the middle of it, juggling her life and the lives of others that she likes (and, maybe, dislikes). She's desperate for good luck, her whole life has been "grab it before somebody else does", "finders keepers", and she slowly realizes throughout the book that sometimes you don't have to. Sometimes things are given.<br /><br />And more importantly, sometimes things are earned.<br /><br />I appreciate the fact that when the author uses Egyptian words she doesn't explain them (or repeat them in English) like some authors do. Instead, she has the meaning slipped in without you realizing it.<br /><blockquote>"<i>Haut meryt</i>, you are mistaken!" protested Sheftu. "There is no name better remembered or more honored than yours in all the Black Land."<br /><br />"Honor I never cared for - nor fame or riches - then or now. 'Beloved General,' you call me..."</blockquote><br />You almost don't realize when she explains the words, because she doesn't really explain. She just translates subtly.<br /><br />What. An amazing book. Couldn't recommend it more. It's one of the best books I've ever read and that will never change, even though the review might (because it's honestly not a good review if you've read the story - <i>Mara</i> deserves a better review but I suck at writing reviews so...oh well).</span>
  <a data-text-id="430075671076880849" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_16293974" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/16293974" />
    <a title="Sophia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/81116-sophia"><img alt="Sophia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1190613398p2/81116.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/16293974?book_show_action=true">Feb 24, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sophia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sophia" href="/user/show/81116-sophia">Sophia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/81116-sophia?shelf=ya-children-s">ya-children-s</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/81116-sophia?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/81116-sophia?shelf=2008">2008</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer16293974" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5160709203888551344">I loved this in junior high and dug it out again for a "light" read -- it's actually more intense than I remembered, but still fun. For being written in 1953, Mara is a surprisingly strong female character, a slave-turned-spy for two opposing masters. She's smart, quick on her feet, speaks Babylonian, plays both sides, and even stands up under torture. The romance novel aspects are the least interesting elements, not because they're particularly silly but just because McGraw's beautiful descript</span>
  <span id="freeText5160709203888551344" style="display:none">I loved this in junior high and dug it out again for a "light" read -- it's actually more intense than I remembered, but still fun. For being written in 1953, Mara is a surprisingly strong female character, a slave-turned-spy for two opposing masters. She's smart, quick on her feet, speaks Babylonian, plays both sides, and even stands up under torture. The romance novel aspects are the least interesting elements, not because they're particularly silly but just because McGraw's beautiful descriptions of ancient Eygpt's people, lands, and politics are so engaging it's hard to pay attention to the romance. It's irritating that Hatshepsut has been turned into the evil villainess, and the "fettered king" whose revolution is being planned isn't described as, ahem, her half-brother and husband (who didn't need a revolution), so it's easier just to read the story as entirely made up. Definitely recommended, even if one of the last lines in the story is "Oh, Amon! No hand but mine shall slay that misbegotten Libyan!"</span>
  <a data-text-id="5160709203888551344" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1282209017" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1282209017" />
    <a title="Schuyler" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7481557-schuyler"><img alt="Schuyler" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1542479008p2/7481557.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1282209017?book_show_action=true">May 16, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Schuyler" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Schuyler" href="/user/show/7481557-schuyler">Schuyler</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1282209017" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13722724722371630855">Mara is one of those books that is pure fun to read. All the time you're reading, you're thinking "this is a good story--a lifetime story--this is why I love books". It's spy fiction at its tightest, with tiny clues and grand stakes that all weave together into the delicious combination of suspense that I like to experience. This book has everything from midnight meets to tomb robbing (and breaking the royal seals on the tombs was no joke for an Egyptian).<br/><br/>The characterization gives food for thou</span>
  <span id="freeText13722724722371630855" style="display:none">Mara is one of those books that is pure fun to read. All the time you're reading, you're thinking "this is a good story--a lifetime story--this is why I love books". It's spy fiction at its tightest, with tiny clues and grand stakes that all weave together into the delicious combination of suspense that I like to experience. This book has everything from midnight meets to tomb robbing (and breaking the royal seals on the tombs was no joke for an Egyptian).<br /><br />The characterization gives food for thought, and is far from a rainbow of happiness, but neither is it one of those gut-wrenching tales that leaves you exhausted and glassy-eyed. When I finished, I had the happy, heart-pumping adrenaline of a story well told that didn't try to knock my emotions out of whack at the same time. I was able to do what I love best: read the story without that hangover angst the next day.<br /><br />The Egyptian culture makes for a unique and beautiful setting. I loved the way McGraw combined the little details of clothing, eye paint, gods, food, and nobility. What made her setting even richer was bringing in a Syrian with completely different culture and value system, and contrasting Mara's love for Egypt with the Syrian Inanni's wariness and disgust. Mara considers Inanni's many shawls frumpy and shapeless, while Inanni considers Mara's sheath-like dress immodest and thin. That's a brilliant way to highlight culture details. The setting alone made me happy. In the midst of my love for countless English/Irish/Scottish tales, having something so gripping set in a very different country like Egypt brought new zest and enchantment to the tale.<br /><br />In reading K.M. Weiland's Structuring Your Novel over the weekend, I constantly remembered Mara, and was pleased by how classy the author's plotting was. From a reading perspective it's a joy, from a writer's perspective it's an example worth emulating. It never dragged, but neither was the action cheesy. McGraw never went over the top and never undersold herself. It hit all the correct crisis points naturally, and crescendoed up to a whammer of a climax that delivered the 100% punch I wanted. McGraw got away with using four or five POVs, but none of them were confusing. Every writer who has a book with any kind of drama in it should read Mara. I would put it in a writing class, or even a literature program for the quality of it.<br /><br />As far as the side I'm still thinking about, Mara is a story set completely within a pagan culture. After being used to something like Haggard, which contains at least some mention of Christianity, it left me wondering how to review it when there was nothing to gain a foothold on from my worldview. Mara contains a lot of lying, which I understood in the context of a spy novel. You can't really have a story about a double spy without it. But still, even when it's necessary, I like to think through it.<br /><br />Last week we learned about an Israeli principle called Pikuach Nefesh. One sect of the Pharisees in the Middle East held that loving God and loving their neighbor were the highest commandments. If you had to lie or break the Sabbath to love your neighbor, then the loving came first. In many ways, Mara makes me think of that, as she makes choices to sacrifice for the spies and king she loves. Though I don't think the author had that principle in mind, and I myself have reservations about it, understanding Pikuach Nefesh helped me process this book as a Christian reader. This is how a poor, non-Christian Egyptian girl would realistically act, and I can respect the consistency of her viewpoint without embracing all of her moral choices.<br /><br />In spite of the deceit factor, there are certain things the characters will not do, come torture or whipping or death. They act by their moral code, and they respect it, even if they swear by all the gods of Egypt in the process. Two things that shine clear are patriotism and deep sacrifice for the well-being of Egypt.<br /><br />For readers who like to look out for romance, Mara contains a significant amount. It was a full-blooded, mature romance, not a shallow and saccharine one. But even though it didn't trouble me, some readers may not care for it. :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="13722724722371630855" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jackie B. - Death by Tsundoku" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jackie B. - Death by Tsundoku" href="/user/show/8952328-jackie-b---death-by-tsundoku">Jackie B. - Death by Tsundoku</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1448440045" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer819055489672079946">Let's hear it for strong female protagonists found in books published in 1953!<br/><br/>Also, let's hear it for being able to describe any book in this way: Spies! Intrigue! Plotting! Romance! Gold! Pharoahs! Swashbuckling! Betrayal! Anguish! Drama!<br/><br/>What a captivating story. <br/><br/>Now, first things first. The history isn't quite accurate. But, that's okay. This is historical fiction, right? As long as you can ignore the real events, this is a great story. That said-- truth, or lack there of, does not take away f</span>
  <span id="freeText819055489672079946" style="display:none">Let's hear it for strong female protagonists found in books published in 1953!<br /><br />Also, let's hear it for being able to describe any book in this way: Spies! Intrigue! Plotting! Romance! Gold! Pharoahs! Swashbuckling! Betrayal! Anguish! Drama!<br /><br />What a captivating story. <br /><br />Now, first things first. The history isn't quite accurate. But, that's okay. This is historical fiction, right? As long as you can ignore the real events, this is a great story. That said-- truth, or lack there of, does not take away from this story. A lot happens in a small period of time. <br /><br />Mara encounters many people during her adventures, and I find them all quite intriguing. What made them to intriguing to me was how perspective switched between them all. We really got to understand this plot as it unfolded from many sides. Now, all those sides happened to be the "winning" side, but that's okay. Either way, it really brought depth to the story. For example, Mara is always scheming to try and maintain her double-agent status. She is constantly complimenting herself on how sneaky she is. However, when we see Mara from another perspective-- we learn this isn't 100% the truth. Inanni, the Canaanite princess Mara acts as interpreter for, notices that Mara is acting suspicious. She knows that something is amiss, and we see Mara for what she really is. Yes, crafty. Yes, smart. But flawed. Which is lovely. <br /><br />I recommend this novel to anyone interested in "Spies! Intrigue! Plotting! Romance! Gold! Pharoahs! Swashbuckling! Betrayal! Anguish! " or just YA historical fiction. :) So, hopefully, everyone. </span>
  <a data-text-id="819055489672079946" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <b>oh, to be a young girl living and dreaming in ancient egypt, dangling the lives of two monarchs and the fate of a country in my own calloused palm</b>
</i> <br /><br />mara has always known to look out for herself. as a slave, she knows that her only true ally is herself, and she can never trust or rely on others. she is told that she is unworthy, beneath others, but mara is defiant. she may lack power, but she is not downtrodden and she is not defeated. mara is not content to keep her head down, but she dreams of riches, palaces, and <i>freedom</i>. so, when mara gets a chance to gain all these things she’s dreamed about, she takes it. she is willing to do whatever she must to gain her freedom, even though the risk would her losing her life. mara is thrust into political turmoil, playing the role of double spy for two contenders to the throne. but, rather than choose the side of one of the rulers, she picks her own side. mara is determined to play to both opponents, working the playing field so that no matter who wins the war, she will win herself. mara is ready and willing to play this dangerous game- the problem is, she isn’t the only one playing it. and the more she wins, the more she has to lose.</span>

<div id="review_939304527" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/939304527" />
    <a title="Hana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10571559-hana"><img alt="Hana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1458172215p2/10571559.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/939304527?book_show_action=true">May 16, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hana" href="/user/show/10571559-hana">Hana</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10571559-hana?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10571559-hana?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10571559-hana?shelf=2014-reads">2014-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer939304527" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7319332615394347833">This was great fun and a smooth, easy read--in fact I fairly tore through this one and could not wait to find out what happened.<br/><br/>McGraw knows how to keep the plot moving and her heroine, Mara the slave girl, is spunky, intelligent and conniving enough to be plausible in her new role as a double agent in the royal court. I'm far from being an Egyptologist, but I've traveled to Egypt and spent enough time in the Egyptian galleries of various museums to know that McGraw gets all sorts of little deta</span>
  <span id="freeText7319332615394347833" style="display:none">This was great fun and a smooth, easy read--in fact I fairly tore through this one and could not wait to find out what happened.<br /><br />McGraw knows how to keep the plot moving and her heroine, Mara the slave girl, is spunky, intelligent and conniving enough to be plausible in her new role as a double agent in the royal court. I'm far from being an Egyptologist, but I've traveled to Egypt and spent enough time in the Egyptian galleries of various museums to know that McGraw gets all sorts of little details correct: the right hand to left shoulder salute, the jewelry and clothing, the terrifying tombs in the Valley of the Kings. No one knows what ancient Egyptian sounded like, but McGraw mixes in enough likely phrases to make the dialog quite believable. <br /><br />I knocked off one star because I thought both of Mara's new masters were too casual in their oversight of this 'agent', and not menacing enough; also I wish we had learned more of Mara's past history, especially how she learned to read and move so easily among the upper classes.<br /><br />But no matter, it was a delightful book and definitely rated G for general audiences (except, of course, this is ancient Egypt, so there are oodles of pagan gods and weird burial practices). </span>
  <a data-text-id="7319332615394347833" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/53064507?book_show_action=true">Apr 17, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anne Osterlund" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anne Osterlund" href="/user/show/2232237-anne-osterlund">Anne Osterlund</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer53064507" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16984629136215067499">Mara is a slave girl in Ancient Egypt. Determined to change her fortune and be free. No matter what it takes. When a messenger from Queen Hatshepsut purchases Mara and makes her an offer to spy and act the part of a royal interpreter, our heroine sees her chance.<br/><br/>But then Sheftu, a scribe who is not a scribe, decides he has a hold over her as well and hires her to spy for the King Thutmos III instead. Which Mara realizes is also a chance.<br/><br/>And all these chances add up to . . . something very much o</span>
  <span id="freeText16984629136215067499" style="display:none">Mara is a slave girl in Ancient Egypt. Determined to change her fortune and be free. No matter what it takes. When a messenger from Queen Hatshepsut purchases Mara and makes her an offer to spy and act the part of a royal interpreter, our heroine sees her chance.<br /><br />But then Sheftu, a scribe who is not a scribe, decides he has a hold over her as well and hires her to spy for the King Thutmos III instead. Which Mara realizes is also a chance.<br /><br />And all these chances add up to . . . something very much on the edge of death. Of course, she could sell out Sheftu to the Queen and save her own hide.<br /><br />But what will happen to Egypt if she does?<br /><br />Mara, Daughter of the Nile has EVERYTHING, in my opinion, that makes great historical fiction. A heroine with enough guts to make her every move worth following. A romance with plenty of danger, suspicion, and impossibility to be totally worth it. Enough historical detail to make you feel like you’re living in the time period. And plenty of political drama to keep you turning pages well into the night and beyond.<br /><br />My FAVORITE historical fiction novel.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16984629136215067499" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText10327854159491948387" style="display:none">Great story! Engaging heroine, smart and plucky without being overly sassy and a hero I am absolutely in love with. I love a ruthless, driven, obsessed man that DOES NOT want to be distracted by a pretty girl. There's just something so sweet about watching the poor guy struggle with his feelings. <br /><br />The setting was superb, and since I haven't read a lot of Egyptian anything it was new and refreshing. The secondary characters were fleshed out, interesting and unique. The plot was right up my alley, because I love political intrigue, and there was plenty of that evident here. <br /><br />I sat up late finishing it, hooked from almost the first page. Definitely recommend this to fans of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21060.Crown_Duel__Crown___Court__1_2_" title="Crown Duel (Crown &amp; Court #1-2) by Sherwood Smith" rel="nofollow noopener">Crown Duel</a>. </span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11828657-elevetha?shelf=cons-spies-and-thievery">cons-spies-and-thievery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer392107261" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10688833351609183389">This was an awesome book. Not sure what I was expecting but this exceeded..by a lot. <br/><br/>And was it really my fault that I was imagining the awesome river boat father figure guy that, sadly, I can't remember the name of, as Sam Axe? I think not.<br/><br/>Highly recommended to all.</span>

<div id="review_756409917" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/756409917" />
    <a title="Hannah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8193435-hannah"><img alt="Hannah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1524881582p2/8193435.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/756409917?book_show_action=true">Nov 04, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hannah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hannah" href="/user/show/8193435-hannah">Hannah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8193435-hannah?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer756409917" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15396368713769825174">This book is a lot of fun. I would particularly recommend it to tween/teen girls. It's exactly the sort of romantic adventure I would have loved to death at that age. I still love it now, but that's because there's a little tween girl still living inside of me--a little tween girl who would have been frightened and thrilled by the action and more than a little intrigued by the dashing hero, Sheftu. He's totally the guy young girls dream of having an adventure with. <br/>You can tell the book was writ</span>
  <span id="freeText15396368713769825174" style="display:none">This book is a lot of fun. I would particularly recommend it to tween/teen girls. It's exactly the sort of romantic adventure I would have loved to death at that age. I still love it now, but that's because there's a little tween girl still living inside of me--a little tween girl who would have been frightened and thrilled by the action and more than a little intrigued by the dashing hero, Sheftu. He's totally the guy young girls dream of having an adventure with. <br />You can tell the book was written in the early 20th century. This is mostly good. The overall feel is an appealing mix of Alfred Hitchcock with The Ten Commandments. <br />It's not really a historical book at all, in spite of all the researched details. It's a fairy tale---a dashing twist on Cinderella--and very suspenseful. This is no cozy mystery where you're sure the heroine won't end up getting hurt. The plot is fast-paced, unpredictable, and the reader is never certain of the safety of any of the characters. Danger takes center stage and reigns supreme. In fact, it's a miracle Mara and Sheftu both didn't get killed. The risks they were taking were just incredible. <br />The book is outstanding. There are only a very few flaws I noticed, and I typically mention any flaws I saw in a review, so here goes..<br />1: The Princess Inanni of Canaan is a good character in herself, but the incessant snide commentary on her weight and the weight of her ladies-in-waiting makes the book seem dated and the heroine, Mara, unkind. Weight comments are a problem in a lot of the popular fiction of that era. I felt this hurt Mara's character a little bit. We were told she's a smart girl and remarkably practical. That isn't consistent with vaguely disliking someone because of her weight---the Princess is a useful friend for Mara ( in fact, without her Mara would undoubtedly have died) and a smart girl would know better than to let physical traits get in the way of making friends. <br />2: During a thrilling scene inside a pyramid the hero, Sheftu, hesitates to kill a man who is certain to betray him to the authorities. This didn't feel believable to me. A guy like Sheftu is too tough and too smart to be merciful. He can't afford to be a gentleman when he's also an outlaw and a spy. That's a shame, but it's true, and Sheftu hesitating made him look less convincing as a tough guy.<br /><br />That's enough criticism for one review! <br />To wrap it up...great book, but not perfect. I've yet to find a perfect book, so Mara still gets 5 stars. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15396368713769825174" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Sharla" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11905458-sharla"><img alt="Sharla" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483253687p2/11905458.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/519875761?book_show_action=true">Jan 28, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sharla" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sharla" href="/user/show/11905458-sharla">Sharla</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11905458-sharla?shelf=witty-characters">witty-characters</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer519875761" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3897511399023565304">I love this story. I loved it even more the second time reading it. It is the type of book that I only find once in a blue moon. Immensely intriguing, fast-paced, captivating characters, and edgy yet lighthearted enough to keep me from spending days bemoaning the darkness of mankind.  It took me to ancient Egypt. With all its flowery over the top descriptions (which I loved), it brought me to the bank of the Nile watching the ships sail into the dark. I got see a world ablaze with ambition, hope</span>
  <span id="freeText3897511399023565304" style="display:none">I love this story. I loved it even more the second time reading it. It is the type of book that I only find once in a blue moon. Immensely intriguing, fast-paced, captivating characters, and edgy yet lighthearted enough to keep me from spending days bemoaning the darkness of mankind.  It took me to ancient Egypt. With all its flowery over the top descriptions (which I loved), it brought me to the bank of the Nile watching the ships sail into the dark. I got see a world ablaze with ambition, hope and desperation.<br /><br /><b>Pros:</b><br />The characters are  extremely clever. I love clever characters. You know the saying "you can be too clever"? I think this book perfectly illustrates and refutes that concept.<br /><br />The story flows well, never resting too long in one spot.<br /><br />The setting. It is set in ancient Egypt. That is pretty sweet. Don't argue with me on that. (Actually do argue, I like to argue. It is interesting, I get to hear different opinions. Argue away in the comments. I want to hear it all!)<br /><br />Sheftu &amp; Mara. Talk about romance. Talk about sparks. Talk about chemistry. Talk about two characters with dynamite personalities! These two were well-matched. It was superb clash and contrast between the two. I dislike books where the girl is weak willed, or is stubborn but rather stupid. Or even worse, when a character starts out strong-willed and spirited but they fall in love and turn into a sappy mess. That does not happen here. Instead I found Mara to be not just spirited, but smart and incredibly clever. Sheftu was equally clever and I find nothing so satisfying as witnessing two characters match wits.<br /><br /><b>Cons:</b><br />I would say that it is too short, but that's not true. Making it longer would have lessened this story's potency and made it weaker.<br /><br />I like this book exactly as it is. Read more reviews at: <a href="https://honestavocado.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">honestavocado.wordpress.com</a></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_331741240" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/331741240" />
    <a title="Shantelle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5482096-shantelle"><img alt="Shantelle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1471497290p2/5482096.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/331741240?book_show_action=true">May 17, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shantelle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shantelle" href="/user/show/5482096-shantelle">Shantelle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5482096-shantelle?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5482096-shantelle?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5482096-shantelle?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5482096-shantelle?shelf=read-in-2014">read-in-2014</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer331741240" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11477138973960633877"><i>Mara, Daughter of the Nile</i> was a superb novel. I was surprised and delighted by the depth of the story, the crazy awesomeness of the plot, and... yes, the entire book in and of itself.<br/><br/>A richly historical book to be sure. We explore Egypt and her culture, customs, kings and queens. Of course, this historical depth includes mentions of gods and goddesses, and also a slightly creepy scene down in the tombs of Egypt's dead kings. That I could have done without.<br/><br/>But yes, the overall story was just ver</span>
  <span id="freeText11477138973960633877" style="display:none"><i>Mara, Daughter of the Nile</i> was a superb novel. I was surprised and delighted by the depth of the story, the crazy awesomeness of the plot, and... yes, the entire book in and of itself.<br /><br />A richly historical book to be sure. We explore Egypt and her culture, customs, kings and queens. Of course, this historical depth includes mentions of gods and goddesses, and also a slightly creepy scene down in the tombs of Egypt's dead kings. That I could have done without.<br /><br />But yes, the overall story was just very well done. A fascinating plot, equally fascinating (thought at times radical) characters, and an unexpectedly sweet and even swoon-y romance. :)<br /><br />Mara, who starts out as a thoroughly rebellious slave, was quite proud at times. A little too proud. But as the end of the book came about, you certainly watched her character change to that of something better. She softened, though her wild, passionate spirit remained as steadfast and loyal as ever. Her eventual beloved was quite the mysterious man. Caring one moment, loftily teasing the next, and darkly intense the next. You can't really blame her for falling for him.<br /><br />I don't think I've read a book quite like this before. It was surprising, breathtaking, and quite startling at points. Really a story to keep you hustling back to its pages once you get into it.<br /><br />As I always say, I prefer a strong spiritual theme. -Which <i>Mara, Daughter of the Nile</i> obviously doesn't have. Oh it has religion, but that of the Egyptian legends and whatnot. But I can certainly appreciate it as a very good historical read, and just very good story-writing overall! :) </span>
  <a data-text-id="11477138973960633877" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground">Readers also enjoyed</h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent"><div class='bookCarousel'>
<div class='carouselRow' style='width: 3600px'>
<ul>
<li class='cover' id='bookCover_613497'>
<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/613497.Hittite_Warrior"><img alt="Hittite Warrior" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1348677284l/613497._SX98_.jpg" />
